<div id="review_139604645" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139604645" />
    <a title="Lisa Wolf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4103395-lisa-wolf"><img alt="Lisa Wolf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280855695p2/4103395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139604645?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Wolf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Wolf" href="/user/show/4103395-lisa-wolf">Lisa Wolf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28245250-the-eyes-of-the-dragon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4103395-lisa-wolf?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4103395-lisa-wolf?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139604645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5084238186121024289">The Eyes of the Dragon, as far as I can tell, is one of King's early departures from writing straight-up horror. It's not a horror story at all -- instead, it's fantasy set in a far-off kingdom, where an evil magician is determined to thrust the land into chaos and bloodshed in order to satisfy his own dark purposes.<br/><br/>King Roland the Good is an okay king, kind but not particularly effective, and perhaps a little too under the sway of his advisor, the magician Flagg. Roland has two sons -- his heir</span>
  <span id="freeText5084238186121024289" style="display:none">The Eyes of the Dragon, as far as I can tell, is one of King's early departures from writing straight-up horror. It's not a horror story at all -- instead, it's fantasy set in a far-off kingdom, where an evil magician is determined to thrust the land into chaos and bloodshed in order to satisfy his own dark purposes.<br /><br />King Roland the Good is an okay king, kind but not particularly effective, and perhaps a little too under the sway of his advisor, the magician Flagg. Roland has two sons -- his heir, Peter, and a younger son, Thomas, who grows up in his older brother's shadow, always plagued by feelings of inadequacy and jealousy as he watches Peter grow into a fine, beloved young man. When Flagg's schemes end with Peter falsely imprisoned on charges of murdering his father, Thomas gains the throne, but he's guided in all things by Flagg, who uses Thomas's weakness to destabilize the country. But Peter is strong and smart, and doesn't give up so easily...<br /><br />Such a terrific story! I was completely enthralled by this tale of loyalty, royalty, friendship, betrayal, and the evil that threatens to undermine families and kingdoms. The characters are so well drawn, showing shades of personality and motivation, and finding hidden dimensions in characters that might otherwise seem like a stock type.<br /><br />The Eyes of the Dragon is an excellent adventure -- don't miss it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5084238186121024289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18368217" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18368217" />
    <a title="Werner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/903390-werner"><img alt="Werner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216337931p2/903390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18368217?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Werner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Werner" href="/user/show/903390-werner">Werner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Werner by: </span>
      One of my library co-workers
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18368217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9006323702679381013">Although I read a good deal in the speculative genres in which King characteristically writes, he's never been a "go-to" author for me. (Originally, that was probably part of a broader pattern; I don't generally seek out the work of most other best-selling authors either, because I innately distrust the hype, and prefer to pick my own reading rather than letting other people in effect pick it for me.) But back in my days as a public librarian, I decided that since his work was so popular with th</span>
  <span id="freeText9006323702679381013" style="display:none">Although I read a good deal in the speculative genres in which King characteristically writes, he's never been a "go-to" author for me. (Originally, that was probably part of a broader pattern; I don't generally seek out the work of most other best-selling authors either, because I innately distrust the hype, and prefer to pick my own reading rather than letting other people in effect pick it for me.) But back in my days as a public librarian, I decided that since his work was so popular with the patrons, I should try to cultivate at least a bit of first-hand knowledge of it, just for purposes of readers advisory services. This novel was one a couple of his that I read at that time, recommended to me by a library colleague as works that I might be more apt to like than others more typical of his output. My wife Barb and I actually read it together, and both liked it moderately well. (As is sometimes the case, that puts my rating solidly in the middle of the spectrum in my friend circle, other ratings there ranging from five stars all the way down to one.)<br /><br />This is a capably written, entertaining conventional fantasy, utilizing a low-tech, medieval-like world mostly resembling real-world Europe, in a realm governed by hereditary kingship, and drawing a strong conflict between good and evil. Evil here is incarnated in the malevolent person of the king's wizard, Flagg (a.k.a Randy Flagg the Dark Man, a villain who appears also in several other King works such as <i>The Stand</i>, and who promotes the cause of darkness across various dimensions of the author's fictional multiverse). The plot involves murder, framing the innocent, and intrigue surrounding the royal succession. It's not an especially outstanding or ground-breaking work of its type, IMO, but it's well done for what it is. If it has any particular strong or distinctive point, I'd say that would be its recognition that sometimes people can be manipulated or misled for bad purposes without themselves being bad people as such (something we all tend at times to forget, sometimes at the expense of fairness). Related to this, the characterizations are commendably realistic, and (except for Flagg) believably nuanced.<br /><br />King apparently wrote this originally for his kids, when they were still in grade school. As a result, it doesn't have any particular bad language that I can recall, and not much in the way of sexual content, certainly none of it explicit. (There is an element of implied teenage sex at one point.) Being set in a fantasy world, it lacks the political references that King sometimes inserts into other works (to ensure that everyone has their ideological labels on perfectly straight, apparently), as well as the slurs against evangelicals that he frequently works in when he's using a real-world setting. It's also a much more normally-sized novel, compared to the ultra-thick behemoths that are more typical of his work. Nonetheless, I don't know that I'd characterize it particularly as a children's book; kids and YAs could certainly read it, but the tone, reading level and general vision are such that wouldn't necessarily fall short for adult tastes, either. (As a trigger warning, one of my friend's reviews mentions a scene of animal cruelty. though I don't actually remember that one myself --it's been nearly 30 years since I read the book.) If you're into traditional fantasy, this isn't a must-read, but I don't believe it would disappoint, either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9006323702679381013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_515115203" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/515115203" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/515115203?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451151254" href="/book/show/848162.The_Eyes_of_the_Dragon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=got-in-2013">got-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=mad-scientists">mad-scientists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer515115203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14906975514978953395">3.5<br/><br/><b>“Once, in a kingdom called Delain, there was a King with two sons. Delain was a very old kingdom and it had had hundreds of Kings, perhaps even thousands; when time goes on long enough, not even historians can remember everything.” </b><br/><br/>King used a unique narrative style for this fairy tale, where he flexes his writing muscle and offers something much different than his usual fare. Fans of the Dark Tower series will see some name similarities and tributes here like King Roland (much different pers</span>
  <span id="freeText14906975514978953395" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br /><b>“Once, in a kingdom called Delain, there was a King with two sons. Delain was a very old kingdom and it had had hundreds of Kings, perhaps even thousands; when time goes on long enough, not even historians can remember everything.” </b><br /><br />King used a unique narrative style for this fairy tale, where he flexes his writing muscle and offers something much different than his usual fare. Fans of the Dark Tower series will see some name similarities and tributes here like King Roland (much different personality than our beloved gunslinger) and Flagg, who is as evil as always. Set in historical fantasy-land times, it's a story about two young brothers rising to become Kings while the kingdom is really being ruled by a demented magician.<br /><br />I loved how King tied in two childhood habits into the story later as major game changers. I enjoyed the characterization - Peter and his allies were formidable forces for good, Roland and Thomas among many who struggle between right and wrong, and then finally Flagg - pure evil badassness with his laboratory and potions. It follows fairy-tale tropes with kingdoms, towers, betrayals, and the day old struggle of brotherly love/envy and living up to a father's ideals.<br /><br />It's not gory, but there are disturbing scenes, such as the use of a certain dragon-influenced poison. King again indulges in weird body humor - scenes with the King farting and picking his nose. King does this often so I guess it's a humor he enjoys, although I could have done without some of the scenes. Gross!<br /><br />Overall it's a well written book and easy to follow, but the pacing lags after the first 1/4th. While the story is a good one, there's just not enough action and variances to justify it's length. Not ridiculously long at 380 pages, but my interest started waning.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14906975514978953395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1133824098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133824098" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133824098?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670814589" href="/book/show/655707.The_Eyes_of_the_Dragon">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">King completionists and gluttons for punishment</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Edward by: </span>
      Mom
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133824098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9336435828409986919">I understand that this was many readers' first King book. I understand that this book rests in the hearts of thousands. I understand this is meant to be a fairytale, and that I am not the target audience. I understand all that and I still choose to hate this book. How'd Bobby Brown put it... "It's my prerogative." <br/><br/><i>The Eyes of the Dragon</i> was slightly more bearable this go around because Laddie from <i>Perfect Strangers</i> read it to me, and I highly suggest you take the same route when/if you decide to</span>
  <span id="freeText9336435828409986919" style="display:none">I understand that this was many readers' first King book. I understand that this book rests in the hearts of thousands. I understand this is meant to be a fairytale, and that I am not the target audience. I understand all that and I still choose to hate this book. How'd Bobby Brown put it... "It's my prerogative." <br /><br /><i>The Eyes of the Dragon</i> was slightly more bearable this go around because Laddie from <i>Perfect Strangers</i> read it to me, and I highly suggest you take the same route when/if you decide to tackle this lesser-known fantasy novel. Bronson Pinchot's performance is fantastic, and lends entertainment value to some of the most boring shit King has ever written. There are only three major scenes in the book, and the plot doesn't even begin until a hundred pages in. That would be fine if this book was six- or seven-hundred pages long. But no. It's 380 pages long, with artwork and big-ass font to make the book seem thicker than it actually is. <br /><br />This book ties in very loosely to the Dark Tower books. Delain is mentioned in several DT novels, and Thomas and Dennis's names are dropped in <i>The Waste Lands</i>, but overall, I feel that this one happens outside of Mid-World, in perhaps another inscape that resides off to the side, much like our own whens. <br /><br />In summation: Not quite Young Adult because there's no trials-of-youth theme and nowhere near the quality of King's adult fiction, <i>The Eyes of the Dragon</i> is pretty much impossible to categorize in the King-verse. Recommended to King completionists only.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9336435828409986919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1736999235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736999235" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47499947-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472330594p2/47499947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736999235?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/47499947-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670814589" href="/book/show/655707.The_Eyes_of_the_Dragon">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">King  compltetionists, Older fairy tale lovers who want to feel young again</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47499947-christy?shelf=what-age-group">what-age-group</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47499947-christy?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736999235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3852323780443111167">Well, that was different.<br/><br/>Well written of course. It wasn't bad at all....Just not what I was expecting (or really wanted--see King's reaction to that view below--if we all would have loved this one--we would have missed out "miserably"). Perhaps I would have rated it higher if I knew what was coming....or what age group this is really written for? Or if I was extremely ill in bed slurping down chicken soup and my mom came in to read it to me (and blush at the mention of the King's "iron") Hmmmm.</span>
  <span id="freeText3852323780443111167" style="display:none">Well, that was different.<br /><br />Well written of course. It wasn't bad at all....Just not what I was expecting (or really wanted--see King's reaction to that view below--if we all would have loved this one--we would have missed out "miserably"). Perhaps I would have rated it higher if I knew what was coming....or what age group this is really written for? Or if I was extremely ill in bed slurping down chicken soup and my mom came in to read it to me (and blush at the mention of the King's "iron") Hmmmm. And...there is some to learn about the vile Flagg in this. He's very very old.<br /><br />The most interesting thing about this book was Stephen King's response to it's so-so-reception. He found out most readers didn't want a "fantasy" book from him. <br /><br />It seems he felt "chained" to his desk to write a certain type of book....namely, horror. So....he immediately wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10614.Misery" title="Misery by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Misery</a>, a book about an author being forced to write a type of book he didn't want to. And, ironically, it is one of his most horrific books.....<br /><br />So, I guess his fans won.....but he certainly didn't lose out either. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10614.Misery" title="Misery by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Misery</a> was one of his best book to film adaptations yet. (And I really hope the writing of it helped release his frustration at the ungrateful fantasy readers!)<br /><br /><br />One final thing I heard....it's possible the Syfy channel is doing something with this book... could be interesting.... I'd probably give it a try.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3852323780443111167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1324138556" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1324138556" />
    <a title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words"><img alt="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556809829p2/38658747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1324138556?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words">Evelyn (devours and digests words)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=writing-i-would-love-to-imitate">writing-i-would-love-to-imitate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=unique-story-lines">unique-story-lines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=great-characterization">great-characterization</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=tortured-hero">tortured-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=worldbuilding-for-the-win">worldbuilding-for-the-win</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1324138556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6657698636932759126"><i> Once upon a time, in the kingdom of Delain far away.... </i><br/><br/>Seriously, why didn't this book started that way? I can hear someone in the background barfing at the cheesiness of it but this chick right here <i> lives </i>for that kind of beginning in fairytales. ESPECIALLY in a Stephen King's book. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10611.The_Eyes_of_the_Dragon' title='The Eyes of the Dragon by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Eyes of The Dragon</a> is all things fantasy. Something I have never read from The King of Horror. It's always a big fun to read an author stepping out of his usual comfort zone. And King nailed it!<br/><br/>This book may</span>
  <span id="freeText6657698636932759126" style="display:none"><i> Once upon a time, in the kingdom of Delain far away.... </i><br /><br />Seriously, why didn't this book started that way? I can hear someone in the background barfing at the cheesiness of it but this chick right here <i> lives </i>for that kind of beginning in fairytales. ESPECIALLY in a Stephen King's book. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10611.The_Eyes_of_the_Dragon" title="The Eyes of the Dragon by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Eyes of The Dragon</a> is all things fantasy. Something I have never read from The King of Horror. It's always a big fun to read an author stepping out of his usual comfort zone. And King nailed it!<br /><br />This book may be purely set in a fantastical world but it does has King's usual grit, <b> and lo and behold!</b> The villain in the story is Flagg himself. <br /><br />Part time Royal Advisor, Part time Dark Magician. He whispers into King Roland The Good's ears, making him do as he[Flagg] bids. In a way, Flagg has the upper hand in controlling the whole kingdom. He is practically the ruler. When Peter was born, First son to Queen Sasha and Roland, Flagg felt that his lifelong plans will be thwarted. He sought to destroy the perfect prissy boy and leave the throne ready for his weak-willed little brother, Thomas. The better to control Delain and lead the kingdom into years of bloodshed.<br /><br />I fucking love this book. For so long, I've been searching up and down for a decent fairytale. I loaded myself with Young Adult fairytale retellings hoping it will sate my thirst but even those still left me empty. Meanwhile, this isn't decent. It's fucking great, more like.<br /><br />I love how it's written. (Duh, It's King!) The writing didn't peeved me off the way it did to some people. In fact, I'm really comfortable with Stephen King writing in the narration of a Storyteller. It's like he's directly talking to the readers and it made me feel more connected.<br /><br /><b> I can find no flaws in this book. </b><br /><br />Good writing? Check.<br /><br />Solid characterization? Check.<br /><br />Amazing, spot on world building? Check.<br /><br />High dosage of tensions? Check.<br /><br />Legit villain? Check.<br /><br />Originality? Check.<br /><br />CHECK. CHECK. CHECK .CHECK.<br /><br />My nitpicky brain shut down and for once, I was actually reading words without a pause. I was reading in enjoyment. And that was so fucking great. <br /><br />I didn't miss out on the fact that one of the characters here is named after King's own daughter, Naomi. It's so sweet that he wrote this book for his little girl. That explains a lot of things to me because in some cases, I felt that things were toned down slightly here! <br /><br />I need more grit though and definitely more of Flagg. MORE.<br /><br /><b> 5 stars. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6657698636932759126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1351327160" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1351327160" />
    <a title="Paul Nelson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson"><img alt="Paul Nelson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434048386p2/7553206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1351327160?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Nelson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Nelson" href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson">Paul Nelson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=2015-books-read">2015-books-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1351327160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer595302150780818226">The Eyes of the Dragon is in my book a kid’s fantasy tale and one with a merrily joyous feel good factor, it was all just too nice and goodly good for me. If my only way of escape was to fashion a rope out of strands of napkin, worked on a toy and it was going to take over a year, then I'd have thrown myself out of the tower on day 3, fuck it as they say and goodbye happy ending.<br/> <br/>Flagg is the man in black, the evil magician who's been around for ever, changing faces and involving himself in the </span>
  <span id="freeText595302150780818226" style="display:none">The Eyes of the Dragon is in my book a kid’s fantasy tale and one with a merrily joyous feel good factor, it was all just too nice and goodly good for me. If my only way of escape was to fashion a rope out of strands of napkin, worked on a toy and it was going to take over a year, then I'd have thrown myself out of the tower on day 3, fuck it as they say and goodbye happy ending.<br /> <br />Flagg is the man in black, the evil magician who's been around for ever, changing faces and involving himself in the running of the kingdom of Delain for generations. He poisons the King and sets eldest son Peter up for the fall. A lifetimes imprisonment in the tower and then it's youngest son Thomas who takes over, subtly prodded by our man in black.<br /> <br />Peter is of course a lovely lad who everyone believes is guilty except a few friends, so he sets out to escape using the threads of many napkins tailored into rope, worked on a tiny loom or whatever it was and aaaaaaaah!!!! thunk.<br /> <br />Oh noooo, he's had enough after three weeks and chucked himself out, three hundred foot to the cobbles below. Ah fuck I was just getting into that and he's blown the ending, every goody fantasy trope blown to the wind all from a disappointing lack of endurance. Boys and dolls houses never end well, Oh well surprises all round there, totally unexpected and I have to say, well played.<br /> <br />Truth? Of course not, it all ends exactly as expected in a well written tale of loveliness.<br /><br />A 2.5* rating.<br /><br />Also posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/1250113/the-eyes-of-the-dragon-by-stephen-king">http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="595302150780818226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_754015902" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754015902" />
    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/754015902?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754015902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1919270508889030925">This is one of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King' title='Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stephen King</a>'s fantasy offerings and it is quite delightful. I do not always enjoy adult fairy stories, but this one catches you up into the action and there is nowhere to go except to read and enjoy the whole book. The way the story is told is quite original. The chapters are all different lengths, sometimes just one paragraph, sometimes a normal length. Quite often the author lets the reader know what is going to happen and then goes back to fill in on how it came about that way</span>
  <span id="freeText1919270508889030925" style="display:none">This is one of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a>'s fantasy offerings and it is quite delightful. I do not always enjoy adult fairy stories, but this one catches you up into the action and there is nowhere to go except to read and enjoy the whole book. The way the story is told is quite original. The chapters are all different lengths, sometimes just one paragraph, sometimes a normal length. Quite often the author lets the reader know what is going to happen and then goes back to fill in on how it came about that way. There's an evil wizard, a dragon, Kings, queens and princes and of course a prison cell at the top of a tower. All great stuff! I think one of the reasons I like King so much is that he is unpredictable yet always comes up with the goods.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1919270508889030925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('O2YoigzcJi7MOt2Pg9wvWBMYXJLUHeAjntPmfp+3gTMQYfCJxNrDIpKN+M3uC1imqtOyt1OC5iPihzU32RSkkQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F2juONxHjyppysfnfm/ARMyZf2d9eUXvP4mIsh8sGyQ8bzY7FEFqJjd94qUTuLe6dVKRQvrmQ+9D3Vv7WY8+hg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17228356679210566943">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText17228356679210566943" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17228356679210566943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
